  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText13885830049168468325" style="display:none">Book two of the dazzling Winner's Trilogy is a fight to the death as Kestrel risks betrayal of country for love.<br /><br />The engagement of Lady Kestrel to Valoria’s crown prince means one celebration after another. But to Kestrel it means living in a cage of her own making. As the wedding approaches, she aches to tell Arin the truth about her engagement... if she could only trust him. Yet can she even trust herself? For—unknown to Arin—Kestrel is becoming a skilled practitioner of deceit: an anonymous spy passing information to Herran, and close to uncovering a shocking secret.<br /><br />As Arin enlists dangerous allies in the struggle to keep his country’s freedom, he can’t fight the suspicion that Kestrel knows more than she shows. In the end, it might not be a dagger in the dark that cuts him open, but the truth. And when that happens, Kestrel and Arin learn just how much their crimes will cost them.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1120161047" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6967482366380242907"><b>Marie Rutkoski has upped her game.</b><br/><br/>I was one of that annoying minority who didn't really like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16069030.The_Winner_s_Curse__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___1_' title='The Winner's Curse (The Winner's Trilogy, #1) by Marie Rutkoski' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Winner's Curse</a>. I mean, it was okay, but proved once again that most writers of YA fantasy focus on the flirtations and romancing and forget about pretty much everything else. However, the way that book ended had me curious about the potential new directions of book two...<br/><br/><b>I was right to be curious.</b> I was right to take my chances on the sequel.<br/><br/>This book just has everything. I would liken it to what Ma</span>
  <span id="freeText6967482366380242907" style="display:none"><b>Marie Rutkoski has upped her game.</b><br /><br />I was one of that annoying minority who didn't really like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16069030.The_Winner_s_Curse__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___1_" title="The Winner's Curse (The Winner's Trilogy, #1) by Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Curse</a>. I mean, it was okay, but proved once again that most writers of YA fantasy focus on the flirtations and romancing and forget about pretty much everything else. However, the way that book ended had me curious about the potential new directions of book two...<br /><br /><b>I was right to be curious.</b> I was right to take my chances on the sequel.<br /><br />This book just has everything. I would liken it to what Maas did when she took us from the romantic, fantasy-lite <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527.Throne_of_Glass__Throne_of_Glass___1_" title="Throne of Glass (Throne of Glass, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Throne of Glass</a> to the clever, action-packed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17167166.Crown_of_Midnight__Throne_of_Glass___2_" title="Crown of Midnight (Throne of Glass, #2) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Crown of Midnight</a>. Rutkoski gets vicious in this book. Kestrel must make the hardest of decisions, sacrifice people for the "greater good", and outwit the emperor and his armies. There are no such things as friends and allies in Kestrel's world anymore; the only person she can rely on is herself.<br /><br />It's amazing how much more I liked the relationship between Kestrel and Arin when it was slipped into the background behind all the treason, revenge and backstabbing going on. The moments when they did meet had more love/hate tension and I found myself angsting over what would happen between them. <b>Because this second book is very clearly not a romance and I felt the complete lack of guarantee in a happy ending on every single page.</b><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20443207.The_Winner_s_Crime__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___2_" title="The Winner's Crime (The Winner's Trilogy, #2) by Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Crime</a> is much more tightly-plotted and full of genuine surprises than the first book. I could hardly look away as it zipped along at a wonderful pace, twisting one way and then another. I like how Kestrel is a complex heroine and not wholly good; she's allowed to be selfish and make choices we don't necessarily agree with. <br /><br />I also feel like we got a better sense of Kestrel's intelligence and ability in this book. Now she has bigger concerns than her romance with Arin and high society life, we get to see her plotting, being damn sneaky, and outwitting the emperor. It gave me a new kind of respect for her and I can't wait to see where her story goes.<br /><br />One thing I like a lot about these books is the way each ending has promised a very different kind of story. I only picked up this book because the ending of the last seemed to suggest an entirely new setting and array of problems... and the end of this one does the same. I can already see that the third book will bring something very different. <br /><br /><b>I'm excited to see what that is.</b><br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6967482366380242907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=betrayal">betrayal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=conspiracy">conspiracy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=arranged-marriages">arranged-marriages</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=secrets">secrets</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1142285835" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18050568731053111091"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419630647i/13100325._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='450' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>3.5 stars.</b> Oh la la, well that was unexpected. This sequel is darker, deadlier, less focused on the romance and containing a delicious addition of conspiracy and secrecy. A beautifully surprising change in the plot and its atmosphere.<br/><br/>Kestrel has it in her to rule a country. She is intelligent, fierce, full of courage and never recreant. Now, her abilities are not only evident and admired but necessary. She will marry the prince of Valoria and no one will stop this event from happening. That is w</span>
  <span id="freeText18050568731053111091" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419630647i/13100325._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>3.5 stars.</b> Oh la la, well that was unexpected. This sequel is darker, deadlier, less focused on the romance and containing a delicious addition of conspiracy and secrecy. A beautifully surprising change in the plot and its atmosphere.<br><br>Kestrel has it in her to rule a country. She is intelligent, fierce, full of courage and never recreant. Now, her abilities are not only evident and admired but necessary. She will marry the prince of Valoria and no one will stop this event from happening. That is what has to be done. In everyone’s best interest. But…is it, really? Kestrel’s character is such an easy one to love. Her voice is one people listen to, and I found myself doing the same. She’s the kind of hero others rely on and the author did a fantastic job in making her a memorable one. However, what I found unfortunate for her character and it can even stretch to the plot itself, is how she doesn’t seem to have anyone on her side. Not really. I mean, there’s a hint of trust here and there, but we can see how everything she does, she does it by herself and with her own determination. Some advisement can be given to her, but nothing that will put the other person in a delicate or vulnerable place.<br><br>Indeed, as I swiftly mentioned, there is less romance...but there still is some. Which is definitely not bad. This book would be half its own size if the matter of heart were not involved. And that leads us to Arin. Arin, sincerely, is a character I have always disliked. Not hated, not despised or loathed, just a person I very often found myself growling at and (mentally) shooing away. Aye, his personality has never appealed to me. Do you remember how he was a ‘slave’ in book one? I’m using quotation marks because, hey there *wake up call*, the guy acted like a prince. As if he owned the place. And that, well, hasn’t changed here. It is much more adapted to the context, for sure, but his behaviour <i>and the things he does</i>, oh dear, it will not please many.<br><br>I don’t remember if the first book had such a slow pacing too. This is a <i>very</i> slow read. The kind of slow that, even if you’re trying to read faster, it will not let you. Like there’s a barrier at every coma that obliges you to make a pause. Personifications we have there, but it was all to say that this is a book you have to take your time with. But, you know, I wasn’t actually bothered by its slow pacing. Sure, at moments, I wanted it all to go faster because of how excited I was to learn some things and know what was to happen next but, overall, I dealt with it nicely and got used to getting introduced first, then led slowly and finally put in front of the evidence, subject, matter. While there may not be extraordinary plot twists, the course of events holds multiple *consequences* to some situations and characters that are interesting to witness.<br><br>Could it be that this is better than <i>The Winner's Curse</i>? Well, for me, it is the absence of overwhelming romance that made the reading more enjoyable. For that, I think many will prefer this continuation, but the ever-present frustrating scenes that this book contains – ones that, even though you are watching and hoping they will not turn out the way you know they will, you can’t change their outcome – make that this book, on the love meter, is at the same percentage as the first. Which is okay, because they are both good reads.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="18050568731053111091" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1118265899" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1118265899" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1118265899?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1118265899" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17442763417136999325"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I’m going to miss you when I wake up,” she whispered, because she realized that she must have fallen asleep under the sun. Arin was too real for her imagination. He was a dream.<br/>“Don’t wake up,” he said.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/>I'm standing next to my window,allowing the near summer breeze to caress my face while I try to pull myself together,to ignore the feeling that <b>I was stabbed in the heart by dozens sharp daggers</b>.For your information <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1238111.Marie_Rutkoski' title='Marie Rutkoski' rel='nofollow noopener'>Marie Rutkoski</a>,<b>the daggers would have hurt less</b>.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389196241ra/8003386.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I don’t mind</blockquote></i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText17442763417136999325" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I’m going to miss you when I wake up,” she whispered, because she realized that she must have fallen asleep under the sun. Arin was too real for her imagination. He was a dream.<br>“Don’t wake up,” he said.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>I'm standing next to my window,allowing the near summer breeze to caress my face while I try to pull myself together,to ignore the feeling that <b>I was stabbed in the heart by dozens sharp daggers</b>.For your information <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1238111.Marie_Rutkoski" title="Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">Marie Rutkoski</a>,<b>the daggers would have hurt less</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389196241ra/8003386.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I don’t mind being a moth.I would probably start eating silk if it meant that I could fly.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>But Kestrel couldn't fly.She was trapped in a life full of balls,gowns,gossip,deception,threats and loneliness,a life she chose and accepted if it meant that Arin would be safe.But was he?Both Arin and Kestrel fought really hard to save Herran,each of them in their own way,while a vicious and greedy emperor whose only love seemed to be power tried to undo their efforts.And themselves.Every attempt Arin made to understand why Kestrel sold herself this way was fruitless because Kestrel denied him the truth for his own protection.Caught in a web of lies and betrayals and mistakes that piled up,they had to figure out whether they could trust each other,and the cost of such trust.<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Arin hadn’t fallen asleep on the deck of his strangely still ship, yet, it felt as if he’d been dreaming. As if dreams and memories and lies were the same thing.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20443207.The_Winner_s_Crime__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___2_" title="The Winner's Crime (The Winner's Trilogy, #2) by Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Crime</a> was an <b>excellent sequel</b> to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16069030.The_Winner_s_Curse__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___1_" title="The Winner's Curse (The Winner's Trilogy, #1) by Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Curse</a>.<b>Brutal</b> and <b>tearjerking</b>,but excellent,although there weren't many scenes between Arin and Kestrel.<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1238111.Marie_Rutkoski" title="Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">Marie Rutkoski</a>'s writing is so <b>rich</b>,filled with so many unspoken yet powerful emotions.She presented her heroes' choices and dilemmas with such clarity that I thought it was me the one who eventually had to take matters in my own hands.I suffered with Arin's ignorance of what Kestrel had sacrificed for him and his struggle to understand,the trials he had to go through,the humiliation and the physical pain,and above all his <b>excruciating love</b> for Kestrel.His anger and hatred were just the surface,under which lied the undying love that even urged him to choose her over his own country.I understand why Kestrel wanted to keep him in the darkness,it was the only way to prevent him from doing something that would put in danger his life and his nation,but there were times I wanted to scream,to make her tell him how much he meant to her.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Kestrel saw all of her mistakes,strung in such a crowded,ugly line that it was difficult to tell which one had come first.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I can't stand the thought of Arin giving up on her,it's so overwhelming and painful.I loathed the emperor for what he did to her and Verex,who turned out to be such a sweet and gallant prince.And I hated her father.After all,Kestrel made the wrong choice.<b>She gambled and she lost.</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Sometimes you think you want something,when in reality you need to let it go.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br>The <b>tension</b> and the <b>longing</b> during the entire book crawled beneath my skin,but after that ending I feel numb,unable to think of anything else.I got a lump in my throat and I try really hard to hold back my tears,but I think I will fail soon.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432050886ra/14895913.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Yeah,I failed.</span>

<div id="review_920946253" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/920946253" />
    <a title="Sophia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3766576-sophia"><img alt="Sophia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571753231p2/3766576.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/920946253?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophia" href="/user/show/3766576-sophia">Sophia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer920946253" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2530913565391106175">march 3, 2015<br/>~4:45 p.m. - i went to the bookstore to pick up the book i've been waiting for forever.<br/>~4:50 p.m. - customer service man went to go dig around in the back to find a copy since THEY RUDELY WEREN'T ON ANY SHELF.<br/>~4:56 p.m. - in this glorious minute, i finally held the winner's crime in my hands. <br/>[insert irrelevant things like math homework and eating dinner but also insert relevant thing like reading]<br/>~1:32 a.m. - finished the winner's crime. <br/>~1:40 a.m. - found dead in bedroom.<br/>~1:45 a.m</span>
  <span id="freeText2530913565391106175" style="display:none">march 3, 2015<br />~4:45 p.m. - i went to the bookstore to pick up the book i've been waiting for forever.<br />~4:50 p.m. - customer service man went to go dig around in the back to find a copy since THEY RUDELY WEREN'T ON ANY SHELF.<br />~4:56 p.m. - in this glorious minute, i finally held the winner's crime in my hands. <br />[insert irrelevant things like math homework and eating dinner but also insert relevant thing like reading]<br />~1:32 a.m. - finished the winner's crime. <br />~1:40 a.m. - found dead in bedroom.<br />~1:45 a.m. - specialists concluded that the cause of death was the book in hand and the fact that the CHARACTERS WOULDN'T JUST COMMUNICATE ALREADY OH MY FREAKING JESUS LORD.<br /><br />okay but forreals let's talk about this evil, evil, evil book<br /><br />first off: i don't think it was as good as the winner's curse, and i know i'm in the minority by saying that. <br />BUT HOLD ON let me explain--this book wasn't bad. it was just fine, pretty excellent really. but i thought the first book was <i>perfection</i> and you can't improve upon perfection. <br /><br />this book was definitely not what i was expecting. nothing that i thought was going to happen happened.<br /><br />kestrel, you are the most interesting blend of erudite and abnegation i have ever seen. you make me want to slap you, but only because your choices make my heart hurt and my blood simmer. if i were in your position, i think i might do the same thing, but then again, maybe i'd be too selfish. <br /><br />arin, you stupid, stupid fool. your impatience, your blindness, your EVERYTHING is so frustrating. i want to smack you for not being able to SEE properly. <br /><br />the tension in this book is subtler than in the first book. the first book is very dramatic, almost extravagantly so. the tension in this book is laid in thin layers until it builds to a crushing weight. <br /><br />the writing is gorgeous as usual. i don't think the prose was as tight (?? pithy???) as in the first novel, but i still liked it. <br /><br />the ending sucked. just like the ending of the winner's curse sucked. and i don't mean suck like, "wow, that was just trash." i mean suck like, "where's the nearest cliff because i need to throw myself off of it." marie rutkoski is really good at making you feel like your beloved characters are never going to be able to get a happy ending. rutkoski excels at making you feel nervous for her characters. you'll feel her ostensibly kind hands twist your guts and set your blood on fire. haven't the characters been through enough? is there no mercy in this godforsaken fantasy world? <br /><br />just thinking about this book makes me cry. (i wish i was exaggerating. i'm not. i'm crying as a i write this. don't make fun. i'm very, very sad.)<br /><br />that's all i have to say for now. wake me up when book 3 comes out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2530913565391106175" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1203502068" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1203502068" />
    <a title="Dorreh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22599584-dorreh"><img alt="Dorreh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565727363p2/22599584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1203502068?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dorreh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dorreh" href="/user/show/22599584-dorreh">Dorreh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1203502068" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18083201492587825512">So I reread this book, solely for the purpose of the new copy I got 2 days ago! <br/><br/>I'm a little shocked quite frankly that my rating didn't change after reading this book a second time.<br/><br/>Somewhere along the lines of good and evil, there is a thin band of nothing, I'd like to think of it as betrayal. And I think that was the ultimate theme exploited in this book. Wether it's a true kind of betrayal, one justified by the greater good or one simply because of ones own shortcomings in morality. The book </span>
  <span id="freeText18083201492587825512" style="display:none">So I reread this book, solely for the purpose of the new copy I got 2 days ago! <br /><br />I'm a little shocked quite frankly that my rating didn't change after reading this book a second time.<br /><br />Somewhere along the lines of good and evil, there is a thin band of nothing, I'd like to think of it as betrayal. And I think that was the ultimate theme exploited in this book. Wether it's a true kind of betrayal, one justified by the greater good or one simply because of ones own shortcomings in morality. The book picked off where the winners curse had ended and quite frankly it ended with a bang. Needless to say I hadn't seen that coming. <br /><br />I loved the way the story got a chance to rebuild itself, around a whole new setting and plot. I had a weakness for Arin since the begging but his jumping to imminent conclusions rubbed me the wrong way. It was immensely frustrating. I always loved Krestel, she was a rare gem in the YA female protagonists. Strategic, clever, and incredibly independent. That last bit was the most important really, a character who, unlike most, didn't need to pine over and waddle in self pity for a boy. She was herself, and didn't change for the sake of others approval. I'd like to applaud that! All the characters portrayed were meticulous and either lovable or abhorrent. I'd like to think of that as something only a very talented author can manage.<br /><br />Overall I reread this book when I got a new copy, I left the older one on the plane last year, and didn't have the chance to get it back. Even though I lost my original review, I retread this book in hopes of dealing with the winners kiss better. I recommend this series to anyone who likes well written, fast paced plots, with great characters. (Even the ones who deserve to have their eyes plucked out). </span>
  <a data-text-id="18083201492587825512" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6731156153025334536">i obsessed over <i>‘the winners curse’</i> and this sequel definitely had the potential to also be a 5 star read had it not been the most spectacularly frustrating display of miscommunication i have ever read. good grief, this had me banging my head against a wall. <br/><br/>i understand that characters keep secrets from each other, especially during conflict and when they are opposite sides of the fight. i get it. but that doesnt mean that its not frustrating to see how everything unravels because of it. theres</span>
  <span id="freeText6731156153025334536" style="display:none">i obsessed over <i>‘the winners curse’</i> and this sequel definitely had the potential to also be a 5 star read had it not been the most spectacularly frustrating display of miscommunication i have ever read. good grief, this had me banging my head against a wall. <br /><br />i understand that characters keep secrets from each other, especially during conflict and when they are opposite sides of the fight. i get it. but that doesnt mean that its not frustrating to see how everything unravels because of it. theres only so much disappointment a reader can take. i get the need for opposition in a story, but when the entire book is nothing but opposition, it makes it difficult to enjoy.<br /><br />that being said, this story is still really good. im just praying to the book gods that something positive happens in the next book, because i really dont think my heart can take much more of this. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>

  <span id="freeText539726094831434962" style="display:none">Reread #4<br /><br />————————<br /><br />Reread x3. What a beauty of a book. <br /><br /><br />————————<br /><br />[Actual rating: 4.5] <br />Ugh, the feels! So good!! So much better than the first. The scope of this book got bigger and better. This story had so much more depth to it and was so well written. The plot was tighter, the political elements and its dirty game were stronger, it was darker, more gruesome. The first book is almost tame in comparison. Or is, actually. The characters were more developed and had a lot more layers and intricacy to them. <br /><br />I did not want to put this book down. <br /><br />I absolutely adored Kestrel in this book. We got to see her be more cunning. She's wise. Strong-headed. Intelligent. Opinionated. Selfless and has a mind of her own. I love the way we saw her reason behind things, and how she came to a conclusion. <br /><br />Arin, my love! I don’t know what to say other than how much I adore the guy. His loyalty made his character what it is. <br /><br />Loved reading it for the second time round. Jumping right into the third book.</span>

Get over it! <br><br>Kestrel made the deal with the emperor to marry his son, Verex in order to save the Herranians. She did that at the end of the first book. Now here she is living with them and trying to keep the wedding put off. Verex is a nice guy and isn't too enthused about the wedding either. My arse Jess, I don't like you any more for your stupidity. <br><br>Moving on. <br><br>Kestrel was playing some tricky games with people trying to work out something to make sure everyone was happy. But................................................................................. does anything ever really work. I want to smack everyone. <br><br>Someone better get their act together in the last book before I climb in the book with a flame thrower and set everyone straight! <br><br>I probably left something out but my brain can't think.               <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=damn-pretty-covers">damn-pretty-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=book-boyfriends">book-boyfriends</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=so-happy-i-read-this">so-happy-i-read-this</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1180144432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1912012755960177584"><b>Update:</b> 27/03/2016, waiting for the last book in the trilogy. <br/><br/>The Winner’s trilogy was an unexpected phenomenon for me. I heard about the first book and I went in without any expectation and ended up being absolutely in love. <br/><br/>Not only the writing style is rich but the characters are very loveable. <br/><br/>I like the traditions and just the whole world is quite interesting. The plot is fluid and the twists are on point.<br/><br/>I can’t say much except that I’m freaking excited for the last book. <br/><br/>_________________</span>
  <span id="freeText1912012755960177584" style="display:none"><b>Update:</b> 27/03/2016, waiting for the last book in the trilogy. <br><br>The Winner’s trilogy was an unexpected phenomenon for me. I heard about the first book and I went in without any expectation and ended up being absolutely in love. <br><br>Not only the writing style is rich but the characters are very loveable. <br><br>I like the traditions and just the whole world is quite interesting. The plot is fluid and the twists are on point.<br><br>I can’t say much except that I’m freaking excited for the last book. <br><br>____________________________________________________<br><br><br><b>| ARC kindly provided by Farrar Straus Giroux via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review. Thank you a lot! |</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420429845ra/13223235.gif" width="500" height="245" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>I AM A LIVING MESS</i><br><br><b>I AM JUST A BALL MADE OUT OF MY OWN TEARS</b><br><br><u>Marie, what have you done to me?</u><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422339417ra/13487770.gif" width="500" height="273" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I'm not sure if I can even write a proper review right now, if I'm honest. This has been so so oh so painful I'm afraid I may spoiler something. <br><br>I mean, how can I read <i>“Sometimes you think you want something,” Arin told him, “when what you need is to let it go.”</i> and expect me to be alright? I cannot. It's too much.<br><br>I will, however, say this:<br><br>The Winner's Crime was darker than the first book with a slower rhythm but don't let it fool you because it'll grab you from your ankles and drag you to the bottom of the blackest hole of pain. It's so beautifully written and so well described but when the book's getting to end it seems to go faster, sharper... it leaves you with this yearning.<br><br>And of all the casualties, you feel like one too. I feel like one.<br><br>I'm just speechless.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422339417ra/13487771.gif" width="500" height="231" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>How can I wait until the next book?<br><br>How will I survive?<br><br><i>Kestrel spat blood. “Nothing,” she told the guard. She thought of her father, she thought of Arin. She told her final lie. “I gave him nothing.”</i><br><br>I need to sleep and stop thinking about this damn book so I can rest a little and try to write a better review tomorrow.<br><br>Or maybe I should leave it like it is. <br><br>Maybe I should stop crying.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422339417i/13487772.gif" width="495" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

I.... I....</b> </i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416424410ra/11962610.gif" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> <b>AND... I CAN'T BELIEVE IT...</b> </i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416424410ra/11962612.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> <b>THIS IS HOW YOU REPAY ME??? TEARING MY HEART OUT WITH THAT ENDING???<br><br>(I MUST ADMIT, THE REST OF THE BOOK WAS EPICCCCCCC, A.M.A.Z.I.N.G)</b> </i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416424410ra/11962611.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> <b>DO YOU HAVE ANY IDEA HOW MUCH...</b> </i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416424410ra/11962613.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> <b>OKAY, OKAY, LETS KEEP IT REAL...</b> </i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416424410ra/11962614.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> <b>YOU, MARIE RUTKOSKI, ARE A PHENOMENAL STORY TELLER, I LOVED THIS BOOK AND THE REST OF THE SERIES, IT'S JUST THAT ENDING WAS TOO MUCH FOR MY HEART TO BARE, ESPECIALLY FOR ANOTHER WHOLE YEAR...</b> </i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416424410ra/11962615.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> <b>MY HEART WILL HEAL, AND I WILL LEARN TO TRUST YOU AGAIN, BUT AS OF TODAY...</b> </i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416424410ra/11962616.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> <b>I LOVE YOU THE WINNERS CRIME, EVEN YOUR HEART BREAKING ENDING!! I LOVE EVERY BIT OF YOU!!!</b> </i><br><br><br><i> <b>~~~~~~EDITED REVIEW~~~~~~</b> </i><br><br><i> <b>4.5 Stars</b> </i><br><br>A stunning and absolutely dazzling world of forbidden romance, broken countries, shattered lives, and determined and unforgettable characters, with sizzling plot twist that will have you in dire need of book three. THE WINNER'S CRIME was breathtaking and heartbreakingly wonderful!!<br><br>Beautifully, and elegantly written, THE WINNER'S CRIME enchanted me from the very beginning until the last sentence. I was dazzled by the smooth and fresh writing that flowed with ease and entranced me into a cocoon of pure bliss. In book one I swept away by the unforgettable and truly unique writing that hypnotized me and kept my heart racing until the end. And in this sequel, THE WINNER'S CRIME was no exception to the full lengths of Marie Rutkoski's brilliant writing skills. She has this spellbinding way with words and world making, and character chemistry that is beyond exceptional. She's a mastermind of a storyteller that everyone should have the honor to read!!<br><br>The romance in this book was what I had an issue with. I LOVE Kestrel and Arin. I mean, I am head over heels in love with them as a couple. I think their perfect for each other in just about every way, and bring the best out in each other, and have this electrifying chemistry that sends shock waves through me with each sentence their together.<br><br>BUT... in THE WINNER'S CRIME there is like ZERO ROMANCE!! YES, you heard that right, ZERO ROMANCE!! Well, no I'm lying, there is these really small little scene where their is some type of love between them. But it was forced and shielded by they're new places in their new life, and they were prudent in keeping their distances, even if it hurt them like hell. And it was heartbreaking to say the least, watching such pain and sorrow as they endured the heartache and loss of love! I just REALLY wanted more from their relationship. Even understanding the reasoning of why Marie Rutkoski had them at each others throat whenever they came within 5 feet of each other, but it was still heartbreaking to watch. It was literally tearing my heart and soul out just to read their harsh encounters. And that made me not enjoy this book as much as book one for that reason and that reason alone. I wanted, NO, NEED, more of Kestrel and Arin time, and if we don't get it in book three, oh well I may just have a to take this trilogy and stomp them into the ground with steel toed boats a million times just to feel better! ;)<br><br>But honestly, besides the relationship issue, I LOVED everything else. The plot was terrifyingly wonderful, and the betrayals were beyond shocking, and totally gut-wrenching to watch unfold. The world in court life was like any other political intrigue novel—lies and deception, betrayals and defiance, plotting and scheming, eager courtiers and snobby nobility, all tied up in blood and murder, and evil emperors wanting nothing more but to conquer all and destroy all who oppose him. But this book was so much fun and a huge change from THE WINNER'S CURSE book setting. And I have a feeling that book three is going to be a totally different book setting then either book one or two. And I am SOOOOOOO looking forward to relishing in the explosive finale that will either shatter the Valorians rule, or the Herrani submission, or, just maybe, maybe shatter both worlds and be something totally unpredictable!! I wouldn't put it past Rutkoski to come up with something so shocking an totally unexpected. BRING IT!!!<br><br><i> <b>THE PLOT:</b> </i><br><br><i> <b>***KESTREL***</b> </i><br><br>Engaged to the crown prince of Valoria, Kestrel should be relishing in the most desired man of all their empire, but she's not. Marrying the crown prince is actually the last thing she desires. With her heart belonging to another, but her fate promised to the Valoria empire, she has excepted her future and the sacrifice it's made for the greater good, even if it still hurts like hell...<br><br>Forced into marriage with the prince as a bargaining chip for freeing Herran from the vicious rule the emperor had on the Herrani slaves, Kestrel has finally freed them from his iron grip and malicious way of living. But payed the ultimate price with her hand in marriage. But what really weighs on her is not the loss of her hand in marriage, but her loss of her heart that is owned by Arin, the slave she bought from the slave auction so many months ago. Falling in love with him really was the winner's curse...<br><br>Now living in the imperial palace as the future Queen to the Valorian Empire, Kestrel must play the hand she dealt herself before more questions threaten to arise and shatter her already fragile world. But as also the imperial ambassador to the now independent territory of Herran, and having to work with the new territory and governor that she traded her life for, she's starting to believe she may be in way over her head.<br><br>Kestrel will have to decide just where and who her true loyalties lie, and if she's willing to lay it all on the line for the Herrani people she's already saved once. Or if she's willing to let them all crash and burn under the emperor's cruel wrath...<br><br><i> <b>***ARIN***</b> </i><br><br>Now the Governor to the independent territory of Herran, Arin has his work cut out for him. As a former slave to the war Generals daughter Kestrel, and the blacksmith at their estate, he and the former leader of the Herrani rebellion have taken their home territory of Herran back by force. But keeping it was the challenge, and Arin realized they were fighting a war they couldn't win. So when the imperial emperor offered Herrani their freedom as a self-governed territory with Arin as their governor, it all seem to good to be true. But of course, with no other options he agreed, and unknowingly sealed with it his beloveds fate as the future queen to the imperial empire, and lost her forever....<br><br>With the weight of the whole territory of Herran on his shoulders, and little resource or accesses to the means in keeping his new territory fed, Arin is coming to the horrifying realization of just why the emperor offered his gracious deal when he did. And unless he finds a way to feed his people and quick, they will all fall to illness and starvation, and the emperor will eliminate the whole Herrani race without even going to war. And that is something Arin cannot allow without going down fighting...<br><br>But if the emperor thinks that they'll just roll over and give up, then he has another thing coming. Arin is determined to build he's territory to it's fullest and forge alliances with the neighboring city of Dacran, in hopes of building an army strong enough to withstand the Valorian army's wrath, and finally end the Valorian rule over the Herrani people once and for all. But in Arin's world, nothing is that simple, and he will have to fight to the death if is going to survive this battle. And his love/hate relationship with Kestrel may just be his ultimate downfall...<br><br>THE WINNER'S CRIME was beautifully crafted and enchantingly wonderful!! With it's fine touch of exquisite imperial life, and it's captivating characters that would invade anyone's heart, to it's addicting plot twist and heart-pounding revelations, THE WINNER'S CRIME is a sequel NOT TO BE MISSED!!!<br><br>Overall, if your looking for heart-pounding romance like THE WINNER'S CURSE, you won't find it here. But if you want a thrilling plot, with unforgettable events, and ultimate betrayals, with shattered hearts, and races on the brink of extinction, then THE WINNER'S CRIME will definitely satisfy and some...<br><br><i> <b>NOTE: I received a physical ARC from Macmillan for reviewing purposes! All opinions expressed are my own and are not influenced in any way!</b> </i><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="12465123262659932440" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10691511100652726562">5/5<br/><br/>THIS IS WHAT I WANTED WHEN I PICKED UP THE WINNER’S CURSE.<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2017/01/31/the-winners-crime-review/'>https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br/><br/>This is The Winner’s Curse:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481420293ra/21420436.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>And THIS is The Winner’s Crime: <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481420293ra/21420437.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481420293ra/21420438.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481420293ra/21420439.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481420293ra/21420440.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>In short, THIS BOOK ROCKS. Kestrel makes all de</span>
  <span id="freeText10691511100652726562" style="display:none">5/5<br><br>THIS IS WHAT I WANTED WHEN I PICKED UP THE WINNER’S CURSE.<br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2017/01/31/the-winners-crime-review/">https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br><br>This is The Winner’s Curse:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481420293ra/21420436.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>And THIS is The Winner’s Crime: <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481420293ra/21420437.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481420293ra/21420438.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481420293ra/21420439.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481420293ra/21420440.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>In short, THIS BOOK ROCKS. Arin is sort of just angsty all the time, which is eh, but Kestrel is a TOTAL BADASS. She just made it onto my all-time-favorite female characters list.<br><br><br>This book is yet another YA attempt at striking the balance between general badassery and romance, but this is the best take I’ve ever seen. Kestrel makes all decisions with her loved ones at heart, but she doesn’t let love or emotion hold her back. She’s tormented over any pain she has to cause to anyone, but she’ll do what she has to to become empress so she can have monopoly over decision-making. Basically, she’s terrific and I love her.<br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481420293ra/21420441.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I am very into politics as well, so when I see a YA book that has anything to do with politics, I’m like, count me in! So it was disappointing when the first book in the series was mostly lovey-dovey gross stuff and not the inner workings of a high-fantasy government. But I figured, hey, it was well written and took like two hours to read, so why not the sequel?<br><br><br>And let me tell you, it would not have taken me almost 6 months to pick this one up if I had known how political it was. This put love to the side and talked government, baby. Okay, no, it didn’t put love to the side, but it wasn’t on every page. Okay, yes, it was pretty much on every page, but the two characters spent most of the book apart so it wasn’t AS intolerable.<br><br><br>I’m scared I won’t like the next book as much, but I lowkey want to read it right now. Too bad I don’t have a copy yet.<br><br><br>Bottom line: work through the first book so you can read the hell out of this one. HIGHLY recommend! Best YA I’ve read in a hot second.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1466972827?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink">Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=recommended-fantasy">recommended-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=favorite-couples">favorite-couples</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=favorite-heroines">favorite-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1466972827" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13857705282342607937">If you’re new to this series… you better <u>THANK YOUR LUCKY STARS that all three books are out</u>. Because this? This book. WORST. CLIFFHANGER. EVER.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>Let me tell you a little story about when I first read this book. </i>
</b><br/><br/>Poor Brittney was sick and stuck in her bed for several days last winter. She was all out of books except the first and second book of this series already purchased and waiting. So she started this series. Loved the first book. Was literally flying in the second book because holy batma</span>
  <span id="freeText13857705282342607937" style="display:none">If you’re new to this series… you better <u>THANK YOUR LUCKY STARS that all three books are out</u>. Because this? This book. WORST. CLIFFHANGER. EVER.<br><br><b>
  <i>Let me tell you a little story about when I first read this book. </i>
</b><br><br>Poor Brittney was sick and stuck in her bed for several days last winter. She was all out of books except the first and second book of this series already purchased and waiting. So she started this series. Loved the first book. Was literally flying in the second book because holy batman THE AGNST. Then, the worse cliffhanger known to man happened. Fine fine, she thought, because the third book is only a purchase away. WRONG. Come to find out it was 3 months away from even being released. <br><br>GUYS. It was the worst. It was like being punched in the face. <br><br>Nay. <br><br>More like someone was able to wield the power of Thor's hammer and direct it right at my face. Like, I had to lay down just to process and try and recover.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471642069ra/20085707.gif" width="320px" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Moving on…</i><br><br><b>This. Plot. </b><br><br>Obviously from the description/end of the last book, you can decipher that Kestrel has basically given herself to the Emperor and his son because of the nice little bargain she made to save Arin’s life. And sure, he’d probably riot and come get her IF ONLY HE KNEW. Of course, she made him believe that she wants this and doesn’t want him. And we all know how stubborn Kestrel is.<br><br>My question is... are you prepared for this? <i>(stop here if you would rather not know the general direction of the plot…) </i><br><br>Are you ready for non stop torture about Arin trying to figure out what in the heck Kestrel got herself into and Kestrel doing everything in her power to make sure he doesn’t find out? Are you ready for hurt feelings and a sense of longing for characters to just communicate? While everyone’s life is on the line? And just general torture?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460395660ra/18735287.gif" width="340px" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Just be prepared for feels. I can't even.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1403599443ra/10116422.gif" width="340px" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also, I've never wanted to murder a certain character more in my life.<br><br>Conclusion? I freaking love this series but it was non stop agony. Yes, I recommend. Yes, I want to watch you all SUFFER. <br><br>That is all I have to say right now. <br><br><a href="http://www.herbookishthings.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/herbookishthings/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>

<div id="review_1896156309" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1896156309" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1896156309?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=ya-ya-land">ya-ya-land</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1896156309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14169239773963990722"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>THE WINNER'S CURSE was a great book, with a great plot, and great characters. It was a non-stop thrill-ride of political intrigue, doomed love, and international espionage, all written with far more finesse and flair than you normally find in a YA fantasy novel. Costume fantasy seems to be the new fad in that department, where the "fantasy" aspect of a book serves no purpose other than to be a pretty backdrop for a romance (I am calling </span>
  <span id="freeText14169239773963990722" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>THE WINNER'S CURSE was a great book, with a great plot, and great characters. It was a non-stop thrill-ride of political intrigue, doomed love, and international espionage, all written with far more finesse and flair than you normally find in a YA fantasy novel. Costume fantasy seems to be the new fad in that department, where the "fantasy" aspect of a book serves no purpose other than to be a pretty backdrop for a romance (I am calling you out, COURT OF THORNS AND ROSES).<br><br><br><br>On the other hand, if ever there was a book that suffered from "<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/shelf/show/second-book-syndrome" rel="nofollow noopener">second book syndrome</a>" it is THE WINNER'S CRIME. After helping to grant the Herrani their independence, Kestrel is now a caged bird in the Valorian court, engaged to the son of and under the thumb of the vindictive emperor whose vengeance is slow but always cuts straight to the heart, and who sees nothing wrong with torture or harming the loved ones of those who he wishes ill. <br><br><br><br>The Herrani's independence, meanwhile, is under threat, as are the eastern plains of Dorcan. Arin, the governor of Herran, has his hands full trying to manage his people while also meeting the impossible demands of the Valorians. Despite all this, he also still can't forget his feelings for Kestrel, which fall somewhere on the continuum between love and hate since they're always coming in conflict.<br><br><br><br>The court intrigue I loved in the first book is still here, which is why this book gets such a high rating. Rutkoski is excellent at drawing out suspense, and creating effortlessly complex political drama that feels realistic (and probably mirrors actual historical events - I'm sure her home bookshelf is crammed with historical nonfiction). What annoyed me the most about THE WINNER'S CRIME is the complete 180 in personality both these main characters undergo. Arin starts doubting everything Kestrel every did for him, ever, and seems to conveniently forget any sort of fondness he had for her, while Kestrel becomes a complete victim and drags her feet about while whining about no one likes her. And nobody <i>does </i>like her in this book: an alternate title for WINNER'S CRIME could just as easily be "Everybody Hates Kestrel." I got really, really tired of all the wangst.<br><br><br><br>All qualms aside, though, <i>The Winner's </i>trilogy is a good series (so far, anyway). It's darker than most YA geared towards women dares to be, and is smart and surprisingly fierce. Speaking as someone who is a little burned out on "girls wearing pretty dresses engage in a forbidden fantasy affair"-type novels, WINNER'S was a welcome reprieve.  If you're a fan of POISON STUDY by Maria V. Snyder, or THE BONE SEASON by Samantha Shannon, you'll probably enjoy THE WINNER'S CURSE.<br><br><br><br>3.5 to 4 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="14169239773963990722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1130393817" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1130393817" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1130393817?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=not-as-good-as-i-expected">not-as-good-as-i-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=not-worth-the-hype">not-worth-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=watch-out-for-puddles-of-angst">watch-out-for-puddles-of-angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=derp-moments">derp-moments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=bad-beginning-loved-the-rest">bad-beginning-loved-the-rest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=when-sparks-don-t-fly">when-sparks-don-t-fly</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=girl-squad">girl-squad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=second-book-syndrome">second-book-syndrome</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1130393817" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4656297932557925012"><blockquote>
  <i>"Arin and I are impossible," [Kestrel] said quietly. "Dangerous. It is best that we keep our distance from each other."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Trusted bloggers and reviewers told me and <i>told me</i> I'd love The Winner's Crime. "The stakes are so high," they raved. "It's miles better than its predecessor!", Your heart will be ripped into little-bity shreds!"<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427378703ra/14266957.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The stakes are high, alright, though not in the way you'd think. <br/><br/><b>Stakes: will Kestrel and Arin stop wallowing in self-inflicted angst long enough to have an honest c</b></span>
  <span id="freeText4656297932557925012" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"Arin and I are impossible," [Kestrel] said quietly. "Dangerous. It is best that we keep our distance from each other."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Trusted bloggers and reviewers told me and <i>told me</i> I'd love The Winner's Crime. "The stakes are so high," they raved. "It's miles better than its predecessor!", Your heart will be ripped into little-bity shreds!"<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427378703ra/14266957.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The stakes are high, alright, though not in the way you'd think. <br><br><b>Stakes: will Kestrel and Arin stop wallowing in self-inflicted angst long enough to have an honest conversation?</b> <br><br>You see, last book, Kestrel agreed to marry the prince in exchange for Herran's freedom. Arin thinks she's betrayed him by giving herself to the royal family which enslaved his country and are continuing to enslave others. Kestrel won't tell him the truth because of half-baked reasons, like "for his own good". <br><br>I waited for the big reveal at 25%. I waited for it some more at 50%. Slowly lost hope at 75%. Said the work 'fuck' when I reached the end.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380238788ra/681611.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Their pot of angst is burnt and inedible, ladies and gentleman. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14290364.Champion__Legend___3_" title="Champion (Legend, #3) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">Champion</a> had a similar series of misunderstandings and secrets. Day and June worked it out before the 70-page mark and made out before storming fronts and kicking ass. Angst is like bullshit; it is only tolerable in small quantities.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427378703ra/14266958.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Arin and Kestrel haven't an ounce of common sense between them.</b> Arin has always been stubborn to the point of stupidity in The Winner's Curse. Who can forget his refusal to sing during the slave market, possibly endangering his spy mission? Here, he openly proclaims his love for Kestrel despite knowing she's engaged and they could both be beheaded for crimes against the royal family.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"He wondered when he would stop sharing things he shouldn't. It was a bad habit."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1410619819ra/11131991.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's nice to know some things don't change.<br><br>Kestrel is equally as dumb. Knowing full well the emperor's hard stance and rumors involving her and a certain ex-slave, she walks around, blabbing her sympathies towards the Herrani to loyalists and wearing her heart on her silky sleeve.<br><br><blockquote>
<i>"Elinor frowned. 'Herran is a colony. This is your home.'<br><br>'Herran </i>was<i> a colony. Now it's an independent territory.'<br><br>'By the grace of our emperor.'"</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427057736ra/14170958.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You. Are. A. Strategist. Act like one.<br><br>I didn't start getting invested until 60%. Kestrel and Arin are apart, so unable to make moony-eyes at the other and thinking woe-is-me thoughts, they actually get stuff done. Marie foreshadows beautifully and seeing it all come together almost made up for the plodding first half. <br><br>Arin-Kestrel shippers, be warned that an absolutely devastating event happens to them near the end. Even me who doesn't give a flying fuck about felt a mild twinge of pain for the poor things.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424542583ra/13775012.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The writing is—there's no polite way to say this—<i>painfully awkward</i>. It reads like it was hauled straight from the burner the second it was finished, no edits needed, and express-mailed to her publisher. The handful of great passages are overshadowed by an excess of sentences beginning with pronouns and character names, so it was either "He did this", "She did that" or "There was something-something". Just because it's an ARC doesn't mean I should put up with lazy first-draft writing.<br><br>The Winner's Curse also seems to be in love with great, sweeping cinematic effects when its characters are in the throes of despair and confusion. Twice, it rains when Arin is talking about Important Things and stops just as he's about to reach an Important Conclusion.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427378703ra/14266959.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Instant sadness. Writers shouldn't need to rely on cheap gimmicks to demonstrate atmosphere. Big-screens have no choice because script-writers and directors can't rely on narration and hidden emotions to do it. An actor can only do so much with his/her body.<br><br>Fairly disappointed overall.<br><br><i>Quotes taken from an uncorrected galley proof and may be subject to change. ARC provided by Netgalley.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4656297932557925012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44125660-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600268807p2/44125660.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1575587502?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/44125660-beth">Beth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44125660-beth?shelf=book-series">book-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44125660-beth?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44125660-beth?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1575587502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6870454691794844471"><b>Bumping this up to 4 Stars!</b><br/><br/><i>He knew it himself. He, too, wanted what he shouldn't. He, too, felt how the heart chooses its own home and refuses reason. Not here, he'd tried to say. Not this. Not mine. Never.</i><br/><br/>So this book for me was completely different from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16069030.The_Winner_s_Curse__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___1_' title='The Winner's Curse (The Winner's Trilogy, #1) by Marie Rutkoski' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Winner's Curse</a> and I'm not saying that's a bad thing! There were a few elements that I really really enjoyed, and some things were so well done and well thought out! In this book though I <i>really really</i> missed the friendship between Arin and</span>
  <span id="freeText6870454691794844471" style="display:none"><b>Bumping this up to 4 Stars!</b><br /><br /><i>He knew it himself. He, too, wanted what he shouldn't. He, too, felt how the heart chooses its own home and refuses reason. Not here, he'd tried to say. Not this. Not mine. Never.</i><br /><br />So this book for me was completely different from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16069030.The_Winner_s_Curse__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___1_" title="The Winner's Curse (The Winner's Trilogy, #1) by Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Curse</a> and I'm not saying that's a bad thing! There were a few elements that I really really enjoyed, and some things were so well done and well thought out! In this book though I <i>really really</i> missed the friendship between Arin and Kestrel, not only that, but the minimal interactions between the pair was also excruciating! (In a way where I <b>wanted more</b>) I knew coming into this, things weren't going to be the same, there had to be lots of changes and lots of deception throughout this book.<br /><br /><i>"You gave me so much once" - Arin</i><br /><br />I had originally put this at a 3.5 star rating, but I've been thinking about this, and it's so much more than what I initially thought. The reason why I didn't mark it as high originally because I thought of all the dishonesty and not being truthful, <b>however</b> that is what this book is made for! <i>It's about playing the game.</i><br /><br />What I enjoyed so much, was the slow burning of this story, as you are told everything that Kestrel does/plans you're screaming at your book for Arin to just make sense of things! I was honestly like YOU CAN DO IT!<br /><br />I'm just going to merge <b>Kestrel and Arin</b> together. Normally I do bit by bit, but they can go together I've decided. I found some things that they both did really, really frustrating in this book. One of my biggest peeves is that Arin murders people in the past and has done in this book and will probably do so in the final book as "sacrifices" however Kestrel does it with good reason and he just doesn't want to know. Do you know what that is? <b>Pot calling the kettle black.</b> This time round we saw the warrior side to both of these characters both overcoming something. I literally cannot wait get properly into the next book! <br /><br />What I <b>liked?</b><br />- The flashbacks used throughout, we got glimpses of the first book, and Arins perspective of this. I thought it was really clever and something a bit different to see more, Arin was such a closed character in the first book, so it was really welcoming to see what he actually felt.<br />- We got to see more characters, I mean I didn't like them <u>all</u> but we got to know more! For example my two favourites were Tensen (I AM WEAK, HE'S SO LOVABLE) and Verex, they're both so kind. One is very very smart, and the other comes across as a humble character but so sweet!<br />- Deliah<br />- <b>All of the deception, it was a delight!</b><br />- THAT ENDING!<br /><b>That bloody letter</b><br />- Okay, can I just say how <b>clever</b> the moth idea was! At first I was like, this is a bit sadistic... BUT what came from it was <u>SUCH</u> a good plan!<br /><br />What <b>didn't I like?</b><br />- Now I know I always say I love to hate a character, but I <u>cannot stand</u> the emperor. He's literally <i>evil.</i><br />- WHO IS TRUSTWORTHY?<br />- Silly as this is, I missed Kestrels friendships with a lot of the characters...<br /><br />So much anticipation for the final book! <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20443235.The_Winner_s_Kiss__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___3_" title="The Winner's Kiss (The Winner's Trilogy, #3) by Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Kiss</a> I'm not ready for you.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1575587444" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Curse</a> - 4 Stars<br /><i>The Winner's Crime - 4 Stars</i><br /><b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1575587516" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Kiss</a> - 4 Stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="6870454691794844471" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
