<div id="review_1283761641" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1283761641" />
    <a title="Jasmine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine"><img alt="Jasmine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582366251p2/21803154.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1283761641?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine">Jasmine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=highly-recommend">highly-recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=ebooks-ibooks">ebooks-ibooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=strong-emotions">strong-emotions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=will-reread">will-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=cliffhanger">cliffhanger</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1283761641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13618905727291664668"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I wanted to trust you,” he whispered. “I tried. But I couldn’t lie to myself hard enough.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I was too absorbed in the story to mark anything in this book so I apologize for the lack of quotes in the following review. :P<br/><br/><i>The Winner's Crime</i> is another fast-paced story with heart-wrenching twists of plot in the trilogy. All I remember is an abundance of political and military strategies among the soldiers and the main characters. Even though there are tons of unpredictable events in this </span>
  <span id="freeText13618905727291664668" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I wanted to trust you,” he whispered. “I tried. But I couldn’t lie to myself hard enough.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I was too absorbed in the story to mark anything in this book so I apologize for the lack of quotes in the following review. :P<br><br><i>The Winner's Crime</i> is another fast-paced story with heart-wrenching twists of plot in the trilogy. All I remember is an abundance of political and military strategies among the soldiers and the main characters. Even though there are tons of unpredictable events in this book, which I absolutely adore, I have to admit that this is my <i>least</i> favorite book among the series. <br><br><b>The reason I don't give it a well deserved 5/5 stars partly because this installment (and the way this story develops) makes the entire plot way <u>too political</u> and partly because I don't really like <u>hearing Kestrel lie anymore.</u> Particularly to Arin and all the people she cares for and vise versa.</b> <br><br>Let's start with the "too political" part. As much as I'm impressed by the idea of "The Winner's Curse" in the first book, I'm aware that this will involve a bit political issues and means. In the beginning, the entire structure of the story isn't obvious enough to see how it'll work out later so I don't feel bothered then. However, I can see the direction more clearly in the sequel and all of Kestrel's political suggestions/lies are formed; the more apparent those characters are on the same page, the stronger the pursuit of power is. Frankly speaking, I dislike politics. So as the story contains too many political issues, I get tired and irksome easily.<br><br>Another disappointment about this book is the fact that Kestrel tells <b>too many lies</b>. I know she's an excellent liar from book one, but she just takes the substance of liar to a whole new level. She lies in the court, lies to her friends, lies to Prince Verex, lies to Arin, lies about the Moth, lies to her father, the emperor, the maids...basically she just lies to everyone in her life. She manipulates them like they're a piece of tile in her faovrite Bite and Sting game. There's few truth weaved through many, many layers of white lies. So it's annoying for me to see those who care so much about her are pathetically fooled. <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“This voice you’ve been using, that bright one… do you think I don’t recognize it? It’s the sound of you laying a trap. Of you hiding behind your own words. And I know that the way you’ve been talking is not you. Say what you want about me, about what happened between us, about the shape of the sun and the color of the grass and any other truths in this world you want to deny. Deny everything until the gods strike you down. But you can’t say that I don’t know you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Overall, despite the above shortcomings, I still have a great time reading this sequel and the next one, The Winner's Kiss, is what I've been looking for all the time. Hence, I highly recommend The Winner's Trilogy to everyone of you. :) <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467178846i/19560612._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13618905727291664668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1025012059" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1025012059" />
    <a title="Rebekah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2669249-rebekah"><img alt="Rebekah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554772145p2/2669249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1025012059?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebekah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebekah" href="/user/show/2669249-rebekah">Rebekah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669249-rebekah?shelf=ya-addiction">ya-addiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669249-rebekah?shelf=clean">clean</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669249-rebekah?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669249-rebekah?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1025012059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3736383142283898533">Oh the FEELS!!! Wow. Just. Wow. If you have read book one which is The Winner's Curse then you need to stop reading this, right now, pick up book one and read these 2 books. They are a MUST OWN, A MUST READ. You want a book that has everything? then look no further because this is it. AND THEY ARE CLEAN! There is romance to swoon for, adventure, political intrigue, lies, truths, heart breaks (reader and character), an amazing cast of characters that you just want to kill of and root for!<br/><a href='http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-3GtUiRC_FSk/VKfVDQTtjgI/AAAAAAAAFqc/o0YxWaFMJXw/s1600/6a90af02f0e88e5425f9d5b621fa6724.jpg' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424197945i/13726848._SY540_.jpg' height='320' width='213' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>The </span>
  <span id="freeText3736383142283898533" style="display:none">Oh the FEELS!!! Wow. Just. Wow. If you have read book one which is The Winner's Curse then you need to stop reading this, right now, pick up book one and read these 2 books. They are a MUST OWN, A MUST READ. You want a book that has everything? then look no further because this is it. AND THEY ARE CLEAN! There is romance to swoon for, adventure, political intrigue, lies, truths, heart breaks (reader and character), an amazing cast of characters that you just want to kill of and root for!<br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-3GtUiRC_FSk/VKfVDQTtjgI/AAAAAAAAFqc/o0YxWaFMJXw/s1600/6a90af02f0e88e5425f9d5b621fa6724.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424197945i/13726848._SY540_.jpg" height="320" width="213" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>The story carries on with the engagement of Lady Kestrel to the Valoria's crown prince who you aren't sure if you want to like or just hate. The engagement itself is a problem yet to save those she loves Kestrel cannot tell anyone of the reason behind her engagement for fear of too many people's lives. Yes Kestrel thinks she can play a serious game between life or death for her and those she's trying to protect. When things spin out of control, Kestrel finds herself utterly alone. This book gets zoo utterly twisted you can't put it down!<br><br>I LOVE Kestrel's character even though you want to yell at her, you also cheer her own, ache with her, and hope she knows what she is doing. While surrounded by the gorgeous beauty of a palace and the balls and gowns, Kestrel has to constantly wear different facades in order to protect the ones she loves and herself, yet for how long is she able to uphold it all up and still try to save a people other deem not worth saving?<br><br>Arin...Arin, Arin. You....kinda bothered me in this book. You seemed a little whinny and I wanted to slap you across the head at times, yet I understand what you were trying to do. You just FEEL for Arin throughout this whole book. UGH! Why must life be so complicated!<br><br>New characters come into play and it's mesmerizing to see how they all play in the game that Marie Rutkoski sets up and how you aren't sure if some of them are good or bad.<br><br>This book is different from book one with all the political intrigue that has your mind spinning.<br><br>Overall I loved it and I couldn't put it down, it tugged on my heartstrings and is a must own.<br><br>Sexual Content: mild<br>Violence: mild<br>Drugs/Alcohol: mild/none<br>Language: mild/none</span>

<div id="review_2368556377" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2368556377" />
    <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz"><img alt="Helena of Eretz ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596076376p2/27036454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2368556377?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780374384708" href="/book/show/21469060-the-winner-s-crime">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=greco-roman">greco-roman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=hardback">hardback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2368556377" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer685782752762329781"><b>“I don’t mind being a moth. I would probably start eating silk if it meant that I could fly.”</b><br/><br/>This book took <i>way too long</i> to read and it had absolutely nothing to do with the novel itself. Trying to keep up with my <b>reading</b> in conjunction with my <b>university work</b> is a <b>bloody nightmare</b>! <i>*cries*</i><br/><br/>This was a <i>buddy read</i> with my Aussie mate, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1593618253' rel='nofollow noopener'>Laura</a>! <3 Enjoy your win for now! It’ll be short-lived! MUAHAHA! ;)<br/><br/>Back to this novel, it was <i>just as addicting</i> as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17756559-the-winner-s-curse' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Winner’s Curse</a>. I don’t know how Marie Rutkoski</span>
  <span id="freeText685782752762329781" style="display:none"><b>“I don’t mind being a moth. I would probably start eating silk if it meant that I could fly.”</b><br /><br />This book took <i>way too long</i> to read and it had absolutely nothing to do with the novel itself. Trying to keep up with my <b>reading</b> in conjunction with my <b>university work</b> is a <b>bloody nightmare</b>! <i>*cries*</i><br /><br />This was a <i>buddy read</i> with my Aussie mate, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1593618253" rel="nofollow noopener">Laura</a>! &lt;3 Enjoy your win for now! It’ll be short-lived! MUAHAHA! ;)<br /><br />Back to this novel, it was <i>just as addicting</i> as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17756559-the-winner-s-curse" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner’s Curse</a>. I don’t know how Marie Rutkoski does it, but her writing just <i>hooks you in</i> and grabs a hold of you, refusing to let you go, even for a moment. And I <b>loved every moment</b> of it! Having said that, this was <i>such an improvement</i> upon the first instalment. The plot was better than ever before, and the twists and turns kept surprising me consistently! Gone were the frivolous flirtations and the nonsensical romance. Now, the stakes are even higher and the action makes you perch at the edge of your seat out of worry for your beloved characters. <br /><br /><b>Kestrel</b> is forced to make the <b>hardest of decisions</b> for <i>“the greater good”</i>, by even sacrificing innocent people, since the needs of the many outweigh the needs of the few. She is simultaneously presented with the task of <b>outwitting the Emperor</b>, and even her own father, <b>the General</b> of the Emperor’s armies. <i>Treason</i> runs amok at court as everyone engages in <i>betrayals, deceptions, and revenge</i> to gain the upper hand in the game of <i>politics and power</i>. I didn’t even mind Kestrel and Arin’s secret meetings, where they gathered in order to avoid the ever-watchful and unescapable eyes of the <i>spies</i> creeping about in every corner. <br /><br /><i>“Kestrel saw all of her mistakes, strung in such a crowded, ugly line that it was difficult to tell which one had come first.”</i><br /><br />If anyone happened to miss Kestrel’s obvious intelligence in the first book, Rutkoski portrays it even better here. She’s such a <b>complex heroine</b>, who consistently questions if she is <i>doing the right thing</i>, as she tries to make the choices that will result in the most minimal amount of causalities. <br /><br /><i>“It made no sense. Its senselessness was painful. How had Kestrel become someone who didn’t make sense?”</i><br /><br />Kestrel is such a <b>capable strategist</b>, who isn’t completely consumed with life at court or moping after Arin’s absence. Rather, she is perfectly content when <i>plotting, scheming, and outwitting</i> all of those who oppose her, most especially her future father-in-law, the Emperor. I have so much respect for her as protagonist. I just wish that we saw more like her in YA fantasy. <br /><br />Admittedly, this book barely makes any corrections to the problems that I had over the <b>lack of world-building</b> and the <b>lack of fantasy elements</b> in the previous book, which is the sole reason that this book <i>did not</i> receive a full 5-star rating. <br /><br />In addition, when it comes to YA fantasy, I need to be fully invested in the entire principal cast, in order to give it the highest rating…and I’m still of the opinion that <b>Arin</b> is <b>bloody useless</b>. He’s <i>naïve, obsessive, and impulsive</i> – the exact opposite of Kestrel, which is why I just can’t picture them as a couple. <b>Friends?</b> <i>Yes.</i> <b>Lovers?</b> <i>No.</i> <br /><br />I was hard-core shipping <b>Kestrel and Verex</b>, her future husband, on the other hand (Yes, I know; he cares for someone else, but tell that to my heart. It’s got other ideas :P). Verex was so <i>genuine, sweet, and kind</i>, that I found him to be such an endearing character. I have a pretty good idea about who Kestrel is destined to be with, but that doesn’t mean that I have to be happy about it… :-/<br /><br />The <b>cliffhanger</b> absolutely killed me and if Kestrel doesn’t make it out, unscathed, I might actually hurt someone! No one hurts my baby, Kestrel! <b>NO ONE!</b> <i>*insert angry face here*</i> Kestrel’s father could also choke for all I care. His consistent treatment of his daughter is awful and he has absolutely no concept of <i>familial loyalty</i>. She constantly tries to help and protect him, but I guess that it doesn’t matter to him. Ugh. What a pathetic excuse for a father. <br /><br />Well, I’m off to begin the third and final book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20443235-the-winner-s-kiss" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner’s Kiss</a>, now, and I hope that it holds up to these amazing first two instalments! :D They have certainly lived up to the hype, thus far!</span>
  <a data-text-id="685782752762329781" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1043991049" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1043991049" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30035966-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523817330p2/30035966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1043991049?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/30035966-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=badass-females">badass-females</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1043991049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6107638240848486069"><b>"I leap without feet to land, my cloth head is filled with sand. I have no wings, yet try to fly... what am I?"... The second and dramatic second book two of The Winner's Curse series perhaps mmmmm.....</b><br/><br/>I was very, very lucky to get an Arc of The Winner's Crime. <br/><br/>I know that when it comes to reading books I only care about one true thing, and that is how the book ends. <b>I REPEAT: IT'S ALL ABOUT THAT ENDING!</b> Doesn't matter if it's the first book or last book in a series. <i>If you don't bring a strong </i></span>
  <span id="freeText6107638240848486069" style="display:none"><b>"I leap without feet to land, my cloth head is filled with sand. I have no wings, yet try to fly... what am I?"... The second and dramatic second book two of The Winner's Curse series perhaps mmmmm.....</b><br /><br />I was very, very lucky to get an Arc of The Winner's Crime. <br /><br />I know that when it comes to reading books I only care about one true thing, and that is how the book ends. <b>I REPEAT: IT'S ALL ABOUT THAT ENDING!</b> Doesn't matter if it's the first book or last book in a series. <i>If you don't bring a strong ending then don't let the door hit ya where the good lord split ya...</i> The thing Marie Rutkoski doesn't disappoint on is book endings. The Winner's Crime is no different.<br /><br />TWC starts off where the first book left off. Krestle is still set to marry the Valoria's crown prince in an ever so awk marriage arrangement. She's still struggling between what is right and what is wrong; who to trust and where her true alliance lies. <i>(Even I still don't know whose side I'm on)</i>. Marie Rutkoski isn't just skilled at book ending she's amazing at dropping oh so subtle hints that are usually closely followed by "WTF" moments. This book is sprinkled like a cupcake with surprises that I can't wait for you all to get a taste of.<br /><br />This book is however very much a second book in a trilogy. It has moments that are a little slower. As usual you know that they are there to lay so much ground work for what will be coming in the next book. The thing I love about this story is Krestle isn't at all your usual suspect as far as ya fem heroines go. She isn't a dagger slinging, muscle having, archery shooting wild women. What she has though is something I think we often overlook in stories, and that is brains. Krestle is oozing with smarts. She has a silver tongue and a quick wit that often lets her see things other over look. This make her even more likeable, believable, and more dangerous than most would think. Arin is still a strong, smart, and very likeable leading male in this novel. And yeah he's still as mysterious and grey eyed as in book one&lt;3. He also may or may not have several sneaky tricks up his borrowed shirt sleeves.<br /><br />Something I absolutely loved about this whole novel is the brief and amazing moment Rutkoski has between Krestle and the father she fears she will never be able to impress. The moment is beautiful and is written to perfection. The thing I really craved was more Arin and Krestle moments. This one didn't have as many as I hope for <b>BUT</b> I'm hoping it's because book three will be overflowing with steamy star-crossed lover-ness and I can be super giddy and heart eyed that whole book. I just want to shake them both and scream <i>"come on and get together already and make beautiful piano playing babies!"</i>. Still the main thing I have to say about this book is <b>THE ENDING THE ENDING THE ENDING!!! IT IS PERFECT</b>, and is worth some of the more book building moments, and slower paced scenes. I have NO doubt that the ending of this series will knock my socks off.<br /><br />feel free to heck out more of our review on <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://southernbredsouthernread.blogspot.com/">http://southernbredsouthernread.blogs...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6107638240848486069" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gs2zhJYroKB7jL3wUmM3uy3aSUXNKSjLyZQ9hFhukG2469pWLXVpyNynCZGllj1k+4WujQOkpqyS6ns1lS1i9w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Kuj+AUaMS/lzTwBEfmsSDlDXzk3F34d4Dckf+8L/XGsQzpfT/dKCkdRktCWJnhjRhogphQtSCR9Wt1lKD7yu8Q==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1238111.Marie_Rutkoski">About Marie Rutkoski</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16069932211091893238">Marie Rutkoski is the <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of The Winner's Trilogy, which begins with <i>The Winner's Curse</i>. She also wrote the YA novel <i>The Shadow Society</i> and the children's fantasy series The Kronos Chronicles, including <i>The Cabinet of Wonders</i>. Her next project is a YA duology set in the same world as <i>The Winner's Curse</i>. The first in this duology is called <i>The Midnight Lie</i> and will be </span>
  <span id="freeText16069932211091893238" style="display:none">Marie Rutkoski is the <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of The Winner's Trilogy, which begins with <i>The Winner's Curse</i>. She also wrote the YA novel <i>The Shadow Society</i> and the children's fantasy series The Kronos Chronicles, including <i>The Cabinet of Wonders</i>. Her next project is a YA duology set in the same world as <i>The Winner's Curse</i>. The first in this duology is called <i>The Midnight Lie</i> and will be published in March 2020. <br /><br />Marie grew up in Bolingbrook, Illinois (a suburb of Chicago), as the oldest of four children. She holds a BA from the University of Iowa and a PhD from Harvard University. Marie is currently a professor at Brooklyn College, where she teaches Renaissance Drama, children's literature and fiction writing. She lives in Brooklyn with her two sons.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/marierutkoski">http://us.macmillan.com/author/marier...</a></span>
